We will continue to provide technical support for NFS for Git repositories throughout 14.x, but we will remove all support for NFS on November 22, 2022. This was originally planned for May 22, 2022, but in an effort to allow continued maturity of Gitaly Cluster, we have chosen to extend our deprecation of support date. Please see our official <a href="https://about.gitlab.com/support/statement-of-support/#gitaly-and-nfs">Statement of Support</a> for further information.</p>
<p>Gitaly Cluster offers tremendous benefits for our customers such as:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/administration/gitaly/#replication-factor">Variable replication factors</a>.</li>
<li><a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/administration/gitaly/#strong-consistency">Strong consistency</a>.</li>
<li><a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/administration/gitaly/#distributed-reads">Distributed read capabilities</a>.</li>
</ul>
<p>We encourage customers currently using NFS for Git repositories to plan their migration by reviewing our documentation on <a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/administration/gitaly/#migrate-to-gitaly-cluster">migrating to Gitaly Cluster</a>.</p>

supported using a single PostgreSQL adapter, whereas the new format is changing to support multiple databases. The <code>main:</code> database needs to be defined as a first configuration item.</p>

We therefore plan to remove support for this authentication method and recommend using the Kerberos <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SPNEGO">SPNEGO</a> integration instead. You can follow the <a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/integration/kerberos/#upgrading-from-password-based-to-ticket-based-kerberos-sign-ins">upgrade instructions</a> to upgrade from the <code>omniauth-kerberos</code> integration to the supported one.</p>

<p>These events have always been disabled by default and had to be manually enabled with a
feature flag. Enabling them can cause too many events to be generated which can
dramatically slow down GitLab instances. For this reason, they are being removed.</p>

`,breaking_change:!0,end_of_support_milestone:"",issue_url:"https://gitlab.com/groups/gitlab-org/configure/-/epics/6",removal_milestone:"15.0",stage:"Configure",tiers:["Core","Premium","Ultimate"],title:"GitLab Serverless",title_plain:"GitLab Serverless"},{announcement_milestone:"14.5",body:`<p>The certificate-based integration with Kubernetes will be <a href="https://about.gitlab.com/blog/deprecating-the-cert-based-kubernetes-integration/">deprecated and removed</a>. As a GitLab.com user, on new namespaces, you will no longer be able to integrate GitLab and your cluster using the certificate-based approach as of GitLab 15.0. The integration for current users will be enabled per namespace.</p>
<p>For a more robust, secure, forthcoming, and reliable integration with Kubernetes, we recommend you use the
<a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/user/clusters/agent/">agent for Kubernetes</a> to connect Kubernetes clusters with GitLab. <a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/user/infrastructure/clusters/migrate_to_gitlab_agent/">How do I migrate?</a></p>
<p>For updates and details about this deprecation, follow <a href="https://gitlab.com/groups/gitlab-org/configure/-/epics/8">this epic</a>.</p>
<p>GitLab Self-Managed customers can still use the feature <a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/update/deprecations/#self-managed-certificate-based-integration-with-kubernetes">with a feature flag</a>.</p>
`,breaking_change:!0,end_of_support_milestone:"",issue_url:"https://gitlab.com/groups/gitlab-org/configure/-/epics/8",removal_milestone:"Pending",stage:"Deploy",tiers:["Free","Premium","Ultimate"],title:"GitLab.com certificate-based integration with Kubernetes",title_plain:"GitLab.com certificate-based integration with Kubernetes"},{announcement_milestone:"14.5",body:`<p>The certificate-based integration with Kubernetes <a href="https://about.gitlab.com/blog/deprecating-the-cert-based-kubernetes-integration/">will be deprecated and removed</a>.</p>
<p>For GitLab Self-Managed, we are introducing the <a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/administration/feature_flags/#enable-or-disable-the-feature">feature flag</a> <code>certificate_based_clusters</code> in GitLab 15.0 so you can keep your certificate-based integration enabled. However, the feature flag will be disabled by default, so this change is a <strong>breaking change</strong>.</p>
<p>For a more robust, secure, forthcoming, and reliable integration with Kubernetes, use the
<a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/user/clusters/agent/">agent for Kubernetes</a> to connect Kubernetes clusters with GitLab.
For information about this migration, see <a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/user/infrastructure/clusters/migrate_to_gitlab_agent/">migrate to agent for Kubernetes</a>.</p>
<p>GitLab will not remove this feature until the new solution has feature parity.

<ul>
<li>The <code>versions</code> field&rsquo;s <code>pipelines</code> field. This returns all the pipelines associated with all the package&rsquo;s versions, which can pull an unbounded number of objects in memory and create performance concerns.</li>
<li>The <code>pipelines</code> field of a specific <code>version</code>. This returns only the pipelines associated with that single package version.</li>
</ul>
<p>To mitigate possible performance problems, we will remove the <code>versions</code> field&rsquo;s <code>pipelines</code> field in milestone 15.0. Although you will no longer be able to get all pipelines for all versions of a package, you can still get the pipelines of a single version through the remaining <code>pipelines</code> field for that version.</p>

Specifically, the following are deprecated:</p>

<li>Requests that have the <code>status</code> field set to <code>approved</code>.</li>

and set to <code>passed</code>. Requests that:</p>
<ul>
<li>Do not contain the <code>status</code> field will be rejected with a <code>422</code> error. For more information, see <a href="https://gitlab.com/gitlab-org/gitlab/-/issues/338827">the relevant issue</a>.</li>
<li>Contain any value other than <code>passed</code> will cause the status check to fail. For more information, see <a href="https://gitlab.com/gitlab-org/gitlab/-/issues/339039">the relevant issue</a>.</li>
</ul>
<p>To align with this change, API calls to list external status checks will also return the value of <code>passed</code> rather than
<code>approved</code> for status checks that have passed.</p>

This extension modifies the validation of GraphQL queries, allowing the use of the <code>ID</code> type for arguments where it would normally be rejected.
Some arguments originally had the type <code>ID</code>. These were changed to specific
kinds of <code>ID</code>. This change may be a breaking change if you:</p>
<ul>
<li>Use GraphQL.</li>
<li>Use the <code>ID</code> type for any argument in your query signatures.</li>
</ul>
<p>Some field arguments still have the <code>ID</code> type. These are typically for
IID values, or namespace paths. An example is <code>Query.project(fullPath: ID!)</code>.</p>
<p>For a list of affected and unaffected field arguments,
see the <a href="https://gitlab.com/gitlab-org/gitlab/-/issues/352832">deprecation issue</a>.</p>
<p>You can test if this change affects you by validating
your queries locally, using schema data fetched from a GitLab server.
You can do this by using the GraphQL explorer tool for the relevant GitLab
instance. For example: <code>https://gitlab.com/-/graphql-explorer</code>.</p>
<p>For example, the following query illustrates the breaking change:</p>

<div class="codeblock-wrapper" data-elastic-exclude>
  <div data-vue-app="codeblock-toolbar" data-code-language="graphql" class="codeblock-toolbar"></div><div class="highlight"><pre tabindex="0" class="chroma"><code class="language-graphql" data-lang="graphql"><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c"># a query using the deprecated type of Query.issue(id:)</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w"></span><span class="c"># WARNING: This will not work after GitLab 15.0</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w"></span><span class="kd">query</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nv">$id</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nc">ID</span><span class="p">!)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">  </span><span class="nc">deprecated</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nc">issue</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="py">id</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nv">$id</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="nc">title</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="py">description</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">  </span><span class="p">}</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w"></span><span class="p">}</span></span></span></code></pre></div></div>
<p>The query above will not work after GitLab 15.0 is released, because the type
of <code>Query.issue(id:)</code> is actually <code>IssueID!</code>.</p>
<p>Instead, you should use one of the following two forms:</p>

<div class="codeblock-wrapper" data-elastic-exclude>
  <div data-vue-app="codeblock-toolbar" data-code-language="graphql" class="codeblock-toolbar"></div><div class="highlight"><pre tabindex="0" class="chroma"><code class="language-graphql" data-lang="graphql"><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c"># This will continue to work</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w"></span><span class="kd">query</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nv">$id</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nc">IssueID</span><span class="p">!)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">  </span><span class="nc">a</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nc">issue</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="py">id</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nv">$id</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="nc">title</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="py">description</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">  </span><span class="p">}</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">  </span><span class="py">b</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nc">issue</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="py">id</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;gid://gitlab/Issue/12345&#34;</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="nc">title</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="py">description</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">  </span><span class="p">}</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w"></span><span class="p">}</span></span></span></code></pre></div></div>
<p>This query works now, and will continue to work after GitLab 15.0.
You should convert any queries in the first form (using <code>ID</code> as a named type in the signature)
to one of the other two forms (using the correct appropriate type in the signature, or using
an inline argument expression).</p>

<a href="https://gitlab.com/gitlab-org/gitlab/-/issues/352517">deprecated</a>. If you currently use a gRPC-aware proxy for

gRPC-aware proxies, even without Gitaly Cluster.</p>

increase throughput and reduce Go garbage collection latency. For more information, see
the <a href="https://gitlab.com/groups/gitlab-com/gl-infra/-/epics/463">relevant epic</a>.</p>

<a href="https://github.com/fluent/fluentd">FluentD</a>,

<p>To integrate these technologies into GitLab, add the desired Helm charts
into your copy of the
<a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/user/clusters/management_project_template/">Cluster Management Project Template</a>.
Deploy these Helm charts in production by calling commands through GitLab
<a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/user/clusters/agent/ci_cd_workflow/">CI/CD</a>.</p>
<p>As part of this change, the following specific capabilities within GitLab
are now deprecated, and are scheduled for removal in GitLab 15.0:</p>
<ul>
<li>The <strong>Security &amp; Compliance</strong> &gt; <strong>Threat Monitoring</strong> page.</li>
<li>The <code>Network Policy</code> security policy type, as found on the <strong>Security &amp; Compliance</strong> &gt; <strong>Policies</strong> page.</li>
<li>The ability to manage integrations with the following technologies through GitLab: AppArmor, Cilium, Falco, FluentD, and Pod Security Policies.</li>
<li>All APIs related to the above functionality.</li>
</ul>
<p>For additional context, or to provide feedback regarding this change,
please reference our open
<a href="https://gitlab.com/groups/gitlab-org/-/epics/7476">deprecation issue</a>.</p>
`,breaking_change:!0,end_of_support_milestone:"",issue_url:"",removal_milestone:"15.0",stage:"Protect",tiers:[],title:"Container Network and Host Security",title_plain:"Container Network and Host Security"},{announcement_milestone:"14.8",body:`<p>The vulnerability check feature is deprecated in GitLab 14.8 and scheduled for removal in GitLab 15.0. We encourage you to migrate to the new security approvals feature instead. You can do so by navigating to <strong>Security &amp; Compliance</strong> &gt; <strong>Policies</strong> and creating a new Scan Result Policy.</p>
<p>The new security approvals feature is similar to vulnerability check. For example, both can require approvals for MRs that contain security vulnerabilities. However, security approvals improve the previous experience in several ways:</p>
<ul>
<li>Users can choose who is allowed to edit security approval rules. An independent security or compliance team can therefore manage rules in a way that prevents development project maintainers from modifying the rules.</li>
<li>Multiple rules can be created and chained together to allow for filtering on different severity thresholds for each scanner type.</li>
<li>A two-step approval process can be enforced for any desired changes to security approval rules.</li>
<li>A single set of security policies can be applied to multiple development projects to allow for ease in maintaining a single, centralized ruleset.</li>
</ul>

<p>We are reducing the number of analyzers used in GitLab SAST as part of our long-term strategy to deliver a better and more consistent user experience.
Streamlining the set of analyzers will also enable faster iteration, better results, and greater efficiency (including a reduction in CI runner usage in most cases).</p>
<p>In GitLab 15.4, GitLab SAST will no longer use the following analyzers:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="https://gitlab.com/gitlab-org/security-products/analyzers/eslint">ESLint</a> (JavaScript, TypeScript, React)</li>
<li><a href="https://gitlab.com/gitlab-org/security-products/analyzers/gosec">Gosec</a> (Go)</li>
<li><a href="https://gitlab.com/gitlab-org/security-products/analyzers/bandit">Bandit</a> (Python)</li>

<div class="alert alert-type-note gl-rounded-lg">
    <div class="alert-icon"></div>
    <div class="gl-min-w-0"><p>This change was originally planned for GitLab 15.0 and was postponed to GitLab 15.4.</p></div>
  </div><p>These analyzers will be removed from the <a href="https://gitlab.com/gitlab-org/gitlab/-/blob/master/lib/gitlab/ci/templates/Security/SAST.gitlab-ci.yml">GitLab-managed SAST CI/CD template</a> and replaced with the <a href="https://gitlab.com/gitlab-org/security-products/analyzers/semgrep">Semgrep-based analyzer</a>.
Effective immediately, they will receive only security updates; other routine improvements or updates are not guaranteed.
After these analyzers reach End of Support, no further updates will be provided.
We will not delete container images previously published for these analyzers; any such change would be announced as a deprecation, removal, or breaking change announcement.</p>
<p>We will also remove Java from the scope of the <a href="https://gitlab.com/gitlab-org/security-products/analyzers/spotbugs">SpotBugs</a> analyzer and replace it with the <a href="https://gitlab.com/gitlab-org/security-products/analyzers/semgrep">Semgrep-based analyzer</a>.
This change will make it simpler to scan Java code; compilation will no longer be required.
This change will be reflected in the automatic language detection portion of the <a href="https://gitlab.com/gitlab-org/gitlab/-/blob/master/lib/gitlab/ci/templates/Security/SAST.gitlab-ci.yml">GitLab-managed SAST CI/CD template</a>. Note that the SpotBugs-based analyzer will continue to cover Groovy, Kotlin, and Scala.</p>
<p>If you&rsquo;ve already dismissed a vulnerability finding from one of the deprecated analyzers, the replacement attempts to respect your previous dismissal. The system behavior depends on:</p>
<ul>
<li>whether you&rsquo;ve excluded the Semgrep-based analyzer from running in the past.</li>
<li>which analyzer first discovered the vulnerabilities shown in the project&rsquo;s Vulnerability Report.</li>
</ul>
<p>See <a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/user/application_security/sast/analyzers/#vulnerability-translation">Vulnerability translation documentation</a> for further details.</p>
<p>If you applied customizations to any of the affected analyzers or if you currently disable the Semgrep analyzer in your pipelines, you must take action as detailed in the <a href="https://gitlab.com/gitlab-org/gitlab/-/issues/352554#breaking-change">deprecation issue for this change</a>.</p>

In the future, only internal IDs (IID) will be supported.</p>
<p>Because GitLab supports multiple work item types, a path such as <code>https://gitlab.com/gitlab-org/gitlab/-/work_items/&lt;global_id&gt;</code> can display, for example, a <a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/user/tasks/">task</a> or an <a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/user/okrs/">OKR</a>.</p>
<p>In GitLab 15.10 we added support for using internal IDs (IID) in that path by appending a query parameter at
the end (<code>iid_path</code>) in the following format: <code>https://gitlab.com/gitlab-org/gitlab/-/work_items/&lt;iid&gt;?iid_path=true</code>.</p>
<p>In GitLab 16.0 we will remove the ability to use a global ID in the work items path. The number at the end of the path will be considered an internal ID (IID) without the need of adding a query parameter at the end. Only the following format will be supported: <code>https://gitlab.com/gitlab-org/gitlab/-/work_items/&lt;iid&gt;</code>.</p>

<p>This Rake task imports a directory tree of repositories into a GitLab instance. These repositories must have been
managed by GitLab previously, because the Rake task relies on the specific directory structure or a specific custom Git setting in order to work (<code>gitlab.fullpath</code>).</p>
<p>Importing repositories using this Rake task has limitations. The Rake task:</p>
<ul>
<li>Only knows about project and project wiki repositories and doesn&rsquo;t support repositories for designs, group wikis, or snippets.</li>
<li>Permits you to import non-hashed storage projects even though these aren&rsquo;t supported.</li>
<li>Relies on having Git config <code>gitlab.fullpath</code> set. <a href="https://gitlab.com/groups/gitlab-org/-/epics/8953">Epic 8953</a> proposes removing support for this setting.</li>
</ul>
<p>Alternatives to using the <code>gitlab:import:repos</code> Rake task include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Migrating projects using either <a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/user/project/settings/import_export/">an export file</a> or
<a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/user/group/import/#migrate-groups-by-direct-transfer-recommended">direct transfer</a> migrate repositories as well.</li>
<li>Importing a <a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/user/project/import/repo_by_url/">repository by URL</a>.</li>
<li>Importing <a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/user/project/import/">repositories from a non-GitLab source</a>.</li>
</ul>

This impacts users on GitLab Self-Managed that have connected their external registry to the GitLab user interface to find, view, and delete container images.</p>
<p>Supporting both the GitLab container registry as well as third-party container registries is challenging for maintenance, code quality, and backward compatibility, and hinders our ability to stay efficient. As a result we will not support this functionality moving forward.</p>
<p>This change will not impact your ability to pull and push container images to external registries using pipelines.</p>
<p>Since we released the new <a href="https://gitlab.com/groups/gitlab-org/-/epics/5523">GitLab container registry</a> version for GitLab.com, we&rsquo;ve started to implement additional features that are not available in third-party container registries. These new features have allowed us to achieve significant performance improvements, such as <a href="https://gitlab.com/groups/gitlab-org/-/epics/8379">cleanup policies</a>. We are focusing on delivering <a href="https://gitlab.com/groups/gitlab-org/-/epics/5136">new features</a>, most of which will require functionalities only available on the GitLab container registry. This deprecation allows us to reduce fragmentation and user frustration in the long term by focusing on delivering a more robust integrated registry experience and feature set.</p>
<p>Moving forward, we&rsquo;ll continue to invest in developing and releasing new features that will only be available in the GitLab container registry.</p>

were introduced in GitLab 15.7. These tokens are more configurable than the old JSON web tokens (JWTs), are OIDC compliant,
and only available in CI/CD jobs that explicitly have ID tokens configured.
ID tokens are more secure than the old <code>CI_JOB_JWT*</code> JSON web tokens which are exposed in every job,
and as a result these old JSON web tokens are deprecated:</p>
<ul>
<li><code>CI_JOB_JWT</code></li>
<li><code>CI_JOB_JWT_V1</code></li>
<li><code>CI_JOB_JWT_V2</code></li>
</ul>
<p>To prepare for this change, configure your pipelines to use <a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/ci/yaml/#id_tokens">ID tokens</a>
instead of the deprecated tokens. For OIDC compliance, the <code>iss</code> claim now uses
the fully qualified domain name, for example <code>https://example.com</code>, previously
introduced with the <code>CI_JOB_JWT_V2</code> token.</p>
<p>In GitLab 15.9 to 15.11, you can <a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/ci/secrets/id_token_authentication/#enable-automatic-id-token-authentication">enable the <strong>Limit JSON Web Token (JWT) access</strong></a>
setting, which prevents the old tokens from being exposed to any jobs and enables
<a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/ci/secrets/id_token_authentication/#configure-automatic-id-token-authentication">ID token authentication for the <code>secrets:vault</code> keyword</a>.</p>
<p>In GitLab 16.0 and later:</p>
<ul>
<li>This setting will be removed.</li>
<li>CI/CD jobs that use the <code>id_tokens</code> keyword can use ID tokens with <code>secrets:vault</code>,
and will not have any <code>CI_JOB_JWT*</code> tokens available.</li>
<li>Jobs that do not use the <code>id_tokens</code> keyword will continue to have the <code>CI_JOB_JWT*</code>
tokens available until GitLab 17.0.</li>
</ul>
<p>In GitLab 17.0, the deprecated tokens will be completely removed and will no longer
be available in CI/CD jobs.</p>

For example, if Sidekiq is currently running with 4 processes (denoted by 4 elements in <code>sidekiq['queue_groups']</code> in <code>/etc/gitlab/gitlab.rb</code>) with queue selector (<code>sidekiq['queue_selector'] = true</code>), you can change Sidekiq to listen to all queues in all 4 processes,for example <code>sidekiq['queue_groups'] = ['*'] * 4</code>. This approach is also recommended in our <a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/administration/reference_architectures/5k_users/#configure-sidekiq">Reference Architecture</a>. Note that Sidekiq can effectively run as many processes as the number of CPUs in the machine.</p>

You need to take care with the migration to avoid losing jobs entirely.</p>

<p>We&rsquo;re reducing the number of supported analyzers used by default in GitLab SAST.
This is part of our long-term strategy to deliver a faster, more consistent user experience across different programming languages.</p>
<p>Starting in GitLab 16.0, the GitLab SAST CI/CD template will no longer use the <a href="https://gitlab.com/gitlab-org/security-products/analyzers/security-code-scan">Security Code Scan</a>-based analyzer for .NET, and it will enter End of Support status.
We&rsquo;ll remove this analyzer from the <a href="https://gitlab.com/gitlab-org/gitlab/-/blob/master/lib/gitlab/ci/templates/Security/SAST.gitlab-ci.yml">SAST CI/CD template</a> and replace it with GitLab-supported detection rules for C# in the <a href="https://gitlab.com/gitlab-org/security-products/analyzers/semgrep">Semgrep-based analyzer</a>.</p>
<p>Effective immediately, this analyzer will receive only security updates; other routine improvements or updates are not guaranteed.
After this analyzer reaches End of Support in GitLab 16.0, no further updates will be provided.
However, we won&rsquo;t delete container images previously published for this analyzer or remove the ability to run it by using a custom CI/CD pipeline job.</p>
<p>If you&rsquo;ve already dismissed a vulnerability finding from the deprecated analyzer, the replacement attempts to respect your previous dismissal. The system behavior depends on:</p>
<ul>
<li>whether you&rsquo;ve excluded the Semgrep-based analyzer from running in the past.</li>
<li>which analyzer first discovered the vulnerabilities shown in the project&rsquo;s Vulnerability Report.</li>
</ul>
<p>See <a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/user/application_security/sast/analyzers/#vulnerability-translation">Vulnerability translation documentation</a> for further details.</p>
<p>If you applied customizations to the affected analyzer, or if you currently disable the Semgrep-based analyzer in your pipelines, you must take action as detailed in the <a href="https://gitlab.com/gitlab-org/gitlab/-/issues/390416#breaking-change">deprecation issue for this change</a>.</p>
<p><strong>Update</strong>: We&rsquo;ve reduced the scope of this change. We will no longer make the following changes in GitLab 16.0:</p>
<ol>
<li>Remove support for the analyzer based on <a href="https://gitlab.com/gitlab-org/security-products/analyzers/phpcs-security-audit">PHPCS Security Audit</a> and replace it with GitLab-managed detection rules in the <a href="https://gitlab.com/gitlab-org/security-products/analyzers/semgrep">Semgrep-based analyzer</a>.</li>
<li>Remove Scala from the scope of the <a href="https://gitlab.com/gitlab-org/security-products/analyzers/spotbugs">SpotBugs-based analyzer</a> and replace it with GitLab-managed detection rules in the <a href="https://gitlab.com/gitlab-org/security-products/analyzers/semgrep">Semgrep-based analyzer</a>.</li>
</ol>
<p>Work to replace the PHPCS Security Audit-based analyzer is tracked in <a href="https://gitlab.com/gitlab-org/gitlab/-/issues/364060">issue 364060</a> and work to migrate Scala scanning to the Semgrep-based analyzer is tracked in <a href="https://gitlab.com/gitlab-org/gitlab/-/issues/362958">issue 362958</a>.</p>

We released these changes in the Latest template versions because they have the potential to disrupt customized CI/CD pipeline configurations.</p>
<p>In all updated templates, we&rsquo;re updating the definition of variables like <code>SAST_DISABLED</code> and <code>DEPENDENCY_SCANNING_DISABLED</code> to disable scanning only if the value is <code>&quot;true&quot;</code>. Previously, even if the value were <code>&quot;false&quot;</code>, scanning would be disabled.</p>

`,breaking_change:!0,end_of_support_milestone:"",issue_url:"https://gitlab.com/gitlab-org/omnibus-gitlab/-/issues/8164",removal_milestone:"17.0",stage:"Enablement",tiers:[],title:"<code>postgres_exporter['per_table_stats']</code> configuration setting",title_plain:"`postgres_exporter['per_table_stats']` configuration setting"},{announcement_milestone:"16.4",body:`<p>The Docker Registry HTTP API V2 Spec, later replaced by the <a href="https://github.com/opencontainers/distribution-spec/blob/main/spec.md">OCI Distribution Spec</a> did not include a tag delete operation, and an unsafe and slow workaround (involving deleting manifests, not tags) had to be used to achieve the same end.</p>
<p>Tag deletion is an important function, so we added a tag deletion operation to the GitLab container registry, extending the V2 API beyond the scope of the Docker and OCI distribution spec.</p>
<p>Since then, the OCI Distribution Spec has had some updates and it now has a tag delete operation, using the <a href="https://github.com/opencontainers/distribution-spec/blob/main/spec.md#deleting-tags"><code>DELETE /v2/&lt;name&gt;/manifests/&lt;tag&gt;</code> endpoint</a>.</p>
<p>This leaves the container registry with two endpoints that provide the exact same functionality. <code>DELETE /v2/&lt;name&gt;/tags/reference/&lt;tag&gt;</code> is the custom GitLab tag delete endpoint and <code>DELETE /v2/&lt;name&gt;/manifests/&lt;tag&gt;</code>, the OCI compliant tag delete endpoint introduced in GitLab 16.4.</p>
<p>Support for the custom GitLab tag delete endpoint is deprecated in GitLab 16.4, and it will be removed in GitLab 17.0.</p>
<p>This endpoint is used by the <strong>internal</strong> container registry application API, not the public <a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/api/container_registry/">GitLab container registry API</a>. No action should be required by the majority of container registry users. All the GitLab UI and API functionality related to tag deletions will remain intact as we transition to the new OCI-compliant endpoint.</p>
<p>If you do access the internal container registry API and use the original tag deletion endpoint, you must update to the new endpoint.</p>

introduced in GitLab 15.9 (renamed from <strong>Limit access <em>to</em> this project</strong> in GitLab 16.3), you can control CI/CD job token access to your project.
When set to <strong>Only this project and any groups and projects in the allowlist</strong>,
only groups or projects added to the allowlist can use job tokens to access your project.</p>
<p>For projects created before GitLab 15.9, the allowlist was disabled by default
(<a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/ci/jobs/ci_job_token/#allow-any-project-to-access-your-project"><strong>All groups and projects</strong></a>
access setting selected), allowing job token access from any project.
The allowlist is now enabled by default in all new projects. In older
projects, it might still be disabled or you might have manually selected
the <strong>All groups and projects</strong> option to make access unrestricted.</p>
<p>Starting in GitLab 17.6, administrators for GitLab Self-Managed and GitLab Dedicated instances can optionally
<a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/administration/settings/continuous_integration/#job-token-permissions">enforce this more secure setting for all projects</a>.
This setting prevents project maintainers from selecting <strong>All groups and projects</strong>.
This change ensures a higher level of security between projects.</p>
<p>In GitLab 18.0, this instance setting will be enabled by default on GitLab.com, GitLab Self-Managed, and GitLab Dedicated.
GitLab Self-Managed and GitLab Dedicated administrators can disable the setting after upgrading to GitLab 18.0
to restore the pre-upgrade behavior. No project settings will be changed in GitLab 18.0 for GitLab Self-Managed and
GitLab Dedicated, though the status of the instance setting impacts all projects on the instance.</p>
<p>To prepare for this change, project maintainers using job tokens for cross-project authentication
should populate their project&rsquo;s <strong>Authorized groups and projects</strong> allowlists. They should then change
the setting to <strong>Only this project and any groups and projects in the allowlist</strong>.</p>
<p>To help identify projects that need access to your project by authenticating with a CI/CD job token, in GitLab 17.6 we also introduced a method to <a href="https://about.gitlab.com/releases/2024/11/21/gitlab-17-6-released/#track-cicd-job-token-authentications">track job token authentications</a> to your projects. You can use that data to populate your CI/CI job token allowlist.</p>
<p>From GitLab 17.10 to 18.6, you can use <a href="https://archives.docs.gitlab.com/18.6/ci/jobs/ci_job_token/#auto-populate-a-projects-allowlist">migration tooling</a> to automatically populate the CI/CD job token allowlist from the job token authentication log. We encourage you to use this migration tool to populate and use the allowlist before <a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/update/deprecations/?removal_milestone=18.0#cicd-job-token-authorized-groups-and-projects-allowlist-enforcement">general enforcement of allowlists in GitLab 18.0</a>. In GitLab 18.0, automatic population and enforcement of the allowlist will occur on GitLab.com as previously announced.</p>
<p>This migration tool <a href="https://gitlab.com/gitlab-org/gitlab/-/work_items/498305">was removed</a> in GitLab 18.7.</p>

This behavior was incorrect because it did not comply with typical shell variable expansion rules. The CI/CD variable reference should expand to only contain the path to the file, not the contents of the file itself. This was <a href="https://gitlab.com/gitlab-org/gitlab/-/issues/29407">fixed for most use cases in GitLab 15.7</a>. Unfortunately, passing CI/CD variables to downstream pipelines was an edge case not yet fixed, but which will now be fixed in GitLab 17.0.</p>
<p>With this change, a variable configured in the <code>.gitlab-ci.yml</code> file can reference a file variable and be passed to a downstream pipeline, and the file variable will be passed to the downstream pipeline as well. The downstream pipeline will expand the variable reference to the file path, not the file contents.</p>
<p>This breaking change could disrupt user workflows that depend on expanding a file variable in a downstream pipeline.</p>

a specific place in a Markdown document or wiki page. But in some edge cases,
the autogenerated anchor is created with fewer dash (<code>-</code>) characters than many users expect.
For example, with a heading with <code>## Step - 1</code>, most other Markdown tools and linters would expect <code>#step---1</code>.
But GitLab generates an anchor of <code>#step-1</code>, with consecutive dashes compressed down to one.</p>
<p>In GitLab 17.0, we will align our autogenerated anchors to the industry standard by no longer stripping consecutive dashes.
If you have Markdown documents and link to headings that could have multiple dashes in 17.0,
you should update the heading to avoid this edge case. With the example above, you
can change <code>## Step - 1</code> to <code>## Step 1</code> to ensure in-page links continue to work.</p>

<a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/user/application_security/continuous_vulnerability_scanning/">continuous vulnerability scanning</a>, to identify their vulnerabilities.</p>
<p>As of GitLab 18.5, this new feature is in Limited Availability. Until the majority of users have migrated to the new dependency scanning feature, GitLab will continue to support the Gemnasium analyzer. Only then,
the Gemnasium analyzer will reach <a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/update/terminology/#end-of-support">end of support</a>.</p>
<p>Due to the significant changes and feature removals this upgrade introduces, it will not be implemented automatically. Existing CI/CD jobs
using the Gemnasium analyzer will continue to function by default to prevent disruption to CI/CD configurations.</p>
<p>Please review the fully detailed changes below and consult <a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/user/application_security/dependency_scanning/migration_guide_to_sbom_based_scans/">the migration guide</a> to assist you with the transition.</p>
<ul>
<li>To prevent disruptions to your CI/CD configuration, when your application uses the stable dependency scanning CI/CD template (<code>Dependency-Scanning.gitlab-ci.yml</code>), dependency scanning uses only the existing CI/CD jobs based on the Gemnasium analyzer.</li>
<li>When your application uses the latest dependency scanning CI/CD template (<code>Dependency-Scanning.latest.gitlab-ci.yml</code>), dependency scanning uses the existing CI/CD jobs based on the Gemnasium analyzer and the new dependency scanning analyzer also runs on the supported file types.
You can also opt-in to enforce the new dependency scanning analyzer for all projects.</li>

<li>The <a href="https://gitlab.com/gitlab-org/security-products/analyzers/gemnasium/">Gemnasium analyzer</a> project is deprecated, as well as the corresponding container images (all tags and variants): <code>gemnasium</code>, <code>gemnasium-maven</code>, <code>gemnasium-python</code>.
These images will not be removed from the GitLab container registry.</li>

If you use S3 object storage for your container registry, and would like to use the new driver sooner, you must update your configuration to use the new <code>s3_v2</code> driver. In GitLab 19.0, the deprecated s3 driver will become an alias for the <code>s3_v2</code> driver, and no manual action will be needed.</p>
<p>The <code>s3_v2</code> storage driver is based on AWS SDK v2 and provides improved performance, better security, and continued support from AWS.
It will be available starting May 2025 to replace the deprecated <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/developer/announcing-end-of-support-for-aws-sdk-for-go-v1-on-july-31-2025/">AWS SDK v1</a>, which reaches end-of-support on July 31, 2025.</p>
<p>The <code>s3_v2</code> driver no longer supports Signature Signing Algorithm v2.
If <code>v4auth: false</code> option is set in the configuration, it will be transparently ignored by the <code>s3_v2</code> driver and the more secure V4 algorithm will be used.
To migrate to the <code>s3_v2</code> driver:</p>
<ol>
<li>Update your registry configuration file to use the <code>s3_v2</code> configuration instead of <code>s3</code>.</li>
<li>Move from Signature Version 2 to Signature Version 4 for authentication if you haven&rsquo;t already, as AWS SDK v2 only supports Signature Version 4.</li>
<li>Test the configuration in a non-production environment before deploying to production.</li>
</ol>
<p>For more information about updating your storage driver configuration, see <a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/administration/packages/container_registry/#use-object-storage">use object storage</a>.</p>

<a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/administration/gitaly/monitoring/#monitor-gitaly-rate-limiting">RPC-based rate limiting</a>
is ineffective. Configuring proper rate limits is challenging and often becomes obsolete quickly because harmful
actions rarely generate enough requests per second to stand out.</p>
<p>Gitaly already supports <a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/administration/gitaly/concurrency_limiting/">concurrency limiting</a> and an
<a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/administration/gitaly/concurrency_limiting/#adaptive-concurrency-limiting">adaptive limiting add-on</a>,
which have proven to work well in production.</p>
<p>Because Gitaly is not directly exposed to external networks and external protection layers, such as load balancers,
provide better safeguards, rate limiting is less effective.</p>
<p>Therefore, we&rsquo;re deprecating rate limiting in favor of the more reliable concurrency limiting. Gitaly RPC-based
rate limiting will be removed in GitLab 18.0.</p>

<p>These bundled Ingress controllers, namely NGINX Ingress, HAProxy, and
Traefik will be dropped from the GitLab Helm chart and GitLab Operator.
Using Ingresses will still be supported by the GitLab Helm chart and GitLab Operator,
but a external Ingress controller must be deployed to do so.</p>
<p>We recommend to migrate to the bundled Envoy Gateway and Gateway API.
Alternatively, you can deploy and configure an
<a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/charts/charts/globals/#configure-ingress-settings">external Ingress controller and class</a>.</p>
`,breaking_change:!0,end_of_support_milestone:"",issue_url:"https://gitlab.com/gitlab-org/gitlab/-/work_items/590799",removal_milestone:"20.0",stage:"systems",tiers:[],title:"Support for NGINX Ingress, HAProxy, and Traefik charts",title_plain:"Support for NGINX Ingress, HAProxy, and Traefik charts"},{announcement_milestone:"18.9",body:`<p>In GitLab 19.0, we plan to remove bundled Mattermost from the Linux package.</p>
<p>Mattermost was first bundled with GitLab in 2015 as an open source team messaging solution, with GitLab SSO included
to support the integration. Since then, Mattermost has significantly matured its own packaging and deployment
options, and adoption of the bundled Mattermost among GitLab customers has remained relatively low.</p>
<p>With Mattermost v11, <a href="https://forum.mattermost.com/t/mattermost-v11-changes-in-free-offerings/25126">Mattermost has deprecated GitLab SSO from their free offering</a>.
Given this change, the maturity of Mattermost standalone deployment options, and the low adoption in our customer
base, we are removing Mattermost from the Linux package.</p>
<p>If you currently use Mattermost bundled with GitLab, refer to
<a href="https://docs.mattermost.com/administration-guide/onboard/migrate-gitlab-omnibus.html">Migrating from GitLab Omnibus to Mattermost Standalone</a>
in the Mattermost documentation for migration instructions and available Mattermost editions.</p>

<p>Support for PostgreSQL 16 is scheduled for removal in GitLab 19.0.
In GitLab 19.0, PostgreSQL 17 becomes the minimum required PostgreSQL version.</p>
<p>PostgreSQL 17 is available as of GitLab 18.9, and you can upgrade at any time before the removal of PostgreSQL 16 in GitLab 19.0.</p>
<p>If you are running a single PostgreSQL instance you installed by using the Linux package, an automatic upgrade may
be attempted with 18.11. Make sure you have enough disk space to accommodate the upgrade.</p>
<p>For more information, see <a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/omnibus/settings/database/#upgrade-packaged-postgresql-server">Upgrade packaged PostgreSQL server</a>.</p>

change.</p>
`,breaking_change:!0,end_of_support_milestone:"",issue_url:"https://gitlab.com/gitlab-org/gitlab/-/work_items/590797",removal_milestone:"19.0",stage:"systems",tiers:[],title:"Support for bundled PostgreSQL, Redis, and MinIO in GitLab Helm chart",title_plain:"Support for bundled PostgreSQL, Redis, and MinIO in GitLab Helm chart"},{announcement_milestone:"18.9",body:`<p>In GitLab 19.0, we are removing <a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/administration/reporting/spamcheck/">Spamcheck</a> from the
Linux package and GitLab Helm chart.</p>
<p>Spamcheck is a service to combat spam on public-facing GitLab instances. By its nature, this feature is primarily
relevant to large public instances, which represents an edge case in our customer base.</p>
<p>Given the low adoption and the availability of standalone deployment options, we are removing Spamcheck from the
Linux package and GitLab Helm chart. Customers not using Spamcheck will not be impacted by this change.
The removal will reduce package size and dependency footprint (and thus security) for the majority of customers.</p>
<p>If you currently use the bundled Spamcheck, you can deploy it separately by using
<a href="https://gitlab.com/gitlab-org/gl-security/security-engineering/security-automation/spam/spamcheck">Docker</a>.</p>
<p>No data migration is required. Configuration guidance is available in the linked documentation.</p>

`,breaking_change:!1,end_of_support_milestone:"",issue_url:"https://gitlab.com/gitlab-org/gitlab/-/issues/601255",removal_milestone:"20.0",stage:"package",tiers:["Premium","Ultimate"],title:"Dependency Proxy for packages is deprecated",title_plain:"Dependency Proxy for packages is deprecated"},{announcement_milestone:"19.1",body:`<p>In GitLab 19.0, the generic <code>stuck_or_timeout_failure</code> and <code>job_execution_timeout</code> job failure reasons were split into a set of more specific reasons (for example, <code>stuck_pending_no_matching_runners</code>, <code>no_updates_running</code>, and <code>server_timeout_running</code>). New builds are no longer recorded with the old reasons.</p>
<p>These old reasons remain valid values for <a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/ci/yaml/#retrywhen"><code>retry:when</code></a> in <code>.gitlab-ci.yml</code>. To avoid silently breaking existing configuration, when you list <code>stuck_or_timeout_failure</code> or <code>job_execution_timeout</code> under <code>retry:when</code>, GitLab treats them as aliases that match the full set of specific reasons that replaced them. GitLab also shows a non-blocking warning in CI lint output and the pipeline editor when these values are used.</p>
<p>Both values are deprecated and scheduled for removal in GitLab 20.0.</p>
<p><strong>Action required:</strong> Update <code>retry:when</code> to use the specific failure reasons instead:</p>
<ul>
<li>Replace <code>stuck_or_timeout_failure</code> with the relevant subset of <code>stuck_pending_with_matching_runners</code>, <code>stuck_pending_no_matching_runners</code>, <code>no_updates_running</code>, and <code>no_updates_canceling</code>.</li>
<li>Replace <code>job_execution_timeout</code> with <code>server_timeout_running</code> and/or <code>server_timeout_canceling</code>.</li>
</ul>

This feature never progressed beyond experimental status.</p>
<p>It will be replaced by a <strong>Go virtual registry</strong>, which will provide a more complete and reliable experience for resolving Go modules through GitLab.</p>
<p><strong>Action required:</strong> If you are using GitLab as a Go module proxy, plan to migrate to the Go virtual registry once it becomes available. In the interim, you may configure an alternative proxy (such as <code>proxy.golang.org</code> or a self-hosted solution) by updating your <code>GOPROXY</code> environment variable.</p>

GitLab features are deprecated and no longer recommended for use.</p><ul><li>Each deprecated feature will be removed in a future release.</li><li>Some features cause breaking changes when they are removed.</li><li>On GitLab.com, deprecated features can be removed at any time during the month leading up to the release.</li><li>To view documentation for a removed feature, see the <a href=https://docs.gitlab.com/archives/>GitLab Docs archive</a>.</li><li>For GraphQL API deprecations, you should <a href=/api/graphql/#verify-against-the-future-breaking-change-schema>verify your API calls work without the deprecated items</a>.</li></ul><p>For advanced searching and filtering of this deprecation information, try
<a href="https://gitlab-com.gitlab.io/cs-tools/gitlab-cs-tools/what-is-new-since/?tab=deprecations">a tool built by our Customer Success team</a>.</p><p><a href=/api/rest/deprecations/>REST API deprecations</a> are documented separately.</p><p><span><svg role="img" aria-label="rss" class="gl-icon s16"><use href="/gitlab_ui/svgs-latest/icons.svg#rss"/><title>rss</title></svg> </span><strong>To be notified of upcoming breaking changes</strong>,
add this URL to your RSS feed reader: <code>https://docs.gitlab.com/releases/breaking-changes.xml</code></p><div data-vue-app=deprecations-list class=gl-mb-7></div><div class="alert alert-type-disclaimer gl-rounded-lg"><div class=alert-icon></div><div class=gl-min-w-0>This page contains information related to upcoming products, features, and functionality.
